       <article class="article page" sc-render-smart-button="false" itemscope> 
        <section class="article-container" data-stats-ve="35">
         <h1>Make your account more secure</h1>
         <div class="article-content-container">
          <div class="cc">
           <p>At Google, we take online security seriously. To protect your Google Account, we strongly recommend following the steps below regularly.</p> 
           <p><strong>Note:</strong> If youre a journalist, activist, or someone else at risk of targeted online attacks, learn about the <a href="https://landing.google.com/advancedprotection/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced Protection Program</a>.</p> 
           <h2><a id="sc" name="sc"></a>Step 1: Do a Security Checkup</h2> 
           <p>Go to <a href="https://myaccount.google.com/security-checkup" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Security Checkup</a> to get personalized security recommendations for your Google Account, including:</p> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy">Add or update account recovery options</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>Your <a href="https://myaccount.google.com/signinoptions/rescuephone?edit" rel="noopener" target="_blank">recovery phone number</a> and <a href="https://myaccount.google.com/recovery/email?edit" rel="noopener" target="_blank">email address</a> are powerful security tools. This contact info can be used to help:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Block someone from using your account without your permission</li> 
              <li>Alert you if theres suspicious activity on your account</li> 
              <li>Recover your account if youre ever locked out</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p>Learn how to <a href="/accounts/answer/183723" rel="noopener">add or change your recovery phone number or email address</a>.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper">
            <a class="zippy" id="2sv" name="2sv">Turn on 2-Step Verification</a> 
            <div> 
             <p><a href="https://myaccount.google.com/signinoptions/two-step-verification" rel="noopener" target="_blank">2-Step Verification</a> helps prevent a hacker from getting into&nbsp;your account, even if they steal your password. To avoid common phishing techniques associated with text message codes, choose a stronger second verification step:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><a href="/accounts/answer/6103523" rel="noopener">Security keys</a> (Most secure verification step)</li> 
              <li><a href="/accounts/answer/7026266" rel="noopener">Google Prompts</a> (More secure than text message codes)</li> 
             </ul> 
             <h3>Increased security: Advanced Protection</h3> 
             <p>If youre a journalist, activist, or someone else at risk of targeted online attacks, consider enrolling in the <a href="https://landing.google.com/advancedprotection/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Advanced Protection Program</a> for a higher level of security. Advanced Protection uses security keys to protect against phishing and includes other protections like blocking unsecure apps.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy"><a id="risky-access" name="risky-access"></a>Remove risky access to your data</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>Consider removing account access for any non-essential apps to better protect sensitive information.</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Manage <a href="https://myaccount.google.com/permissions" rel="noopener" target="_blank">apps with access to your account</a> and <a href="/accounts/answer/3466521">learn more about the risks</a>.</li> 
              <li>Turn off access for <a href="/accounts/answer/6010255" rel="noopener">apps that use less secure sign-in technology</a>.</li> 
             </ul> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy">Turn on screen locks</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>Screen locks help protect your devices from being used without your permission. Learn <a href="/android/answer/9079129">how to set screen locks on an Android device</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>Note:</strong> For info on adding a screen lock on other devices and computers, visit the manufacturers support site.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <h2><a id="software" name="software"></a>Step 2: Update your software</h2> 
           <p>If your browser, operating system, or apps are out-of-date, the software might not be safe from hackers. Keep your software updated to help protect your account.</p> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy">Update your browser</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>Make sure youre using the latest version of&nbsp;your browser.</p> 
             <p>Learn how to <a href="/chrome/answer/95414">update Google Chrome</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>Note:</strong> For info on updating other browsers, visit the developers support site.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy"><a id="os" name="os"></a>Update your operating system</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>Make sure youre using the latest version of the operating system on your device or computer.</p> 
             <div class="no-margin">
              <h3>Update Android devices</h3> 
              <p>Learn how to <a href="/android/answer/7680439">check and update your Android version</a>.</p> 
             </div> 
             <h3>Update Chromebooks</h3> 
             <p>Learn how to <a href="/chromebook/answer/177889">update your Chromebooks operating system</a>.</p> 
             <p><strong>Note:</strong> For info on updating other devices and computers, visit the manufacturers support site.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy"><a id="apps" name="apps"></a>Update your apps</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>Make sure youre using the latest version of the apps on your phone or computer.</p> 
             <div class="no-margin">
              <h3>Update Android apps</h3> 
              <p>Learn how to update your Android apps on <a href="/googleplay/answer/113412">Android devices</a> and compatible <a href="/chromebook/answer/7021273#updateapp">Chromebooks</a>.</p> 
              <p>Consider turning on <a href="/googleplay/answer/113412#auto">automatic app updates</a> for your Android devices to help make sure youre always using the latest version.</p> 
              <p><strong>Note</strong>: For info on updating apps on other devices and computers, visit the manufacturers support site.</p> 
              <h4>Turn on Google Play Protect</h4> 
              <p>Google Play Protect helps keep Android devices safe from harmful apps. Learn how to <a href="/googleplay/answer/2812853">turn on Google Play Protect</a>.</p> 
             </div> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <h2>Step 3: Use unique, strong passwords</h2> 
           <p>Its risky to use the same password on multiple sites. If your password for one site is hacked, it could be used to get into your accounts for multiple sites.</p> 
           <p>Make sure to <a href="/accounts/answer/32040" rel="noopener">create a strong, unique password</a> for each account.</p> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy">Manage your passwords</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>A password manager can help you generate and manage strong, unique passwords. Consider using one from <a href="/accounts/answer/6197437">Chrome</a> or another trusted password manager provider.</p> 
             <p><strong>Tip:</strong> To find out if any passwords saved in your Google Account may be exposed, are weak, or are reused for multiple accounts, you can use <a href="/accounts/answer/9457609" rel="noopener">Password Checkup</a>.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy">Help protect your password from hackers</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>To get notified if you enter your Google Account password on a non-Google site, turn on <a href="/accounts/answer/6206323">Password Alert</a> for Chrome. That way, youll know if a site is impersonating Google, and you can change your password if it gets stolen.</p> 
             <p><strong>Note:</strong> <a href="#2sv" rel="noopener">Turn on 2-Step Verification </a>for an extra layer of account security.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <h2><a id="apps-exts" name="apps-exts"></a>Step 4: Remove apps &amp; browser extensions you dont need</h2> 
           <p>As more apps are installed on a device, it can become more vulnerable. Install only essential apps and browser extensions on devices that have access to sensitive information. Avoid installing unknown apps or apps from unknown sources to protect your device and personal info.</p> 
           <p>Learn how to:</p> 
           <div class="no-margin">
            <ul> 
             <li><a href="/googleplay/answer/2521768">Delete or disable apps on Android devices</a></li> 
            </ul> 
           </div> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="/chrome_webstore/answer/2664769#uninstall-extension">Uninstall extensions on Chrome</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/chromebook/answer/2589434">Uninstall apps or extensions on Chromebooks</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <p><strong>Note:</strong> For info on removing apps and extensions from other devices and browsers, visit the applicable support site.</p> 
           <h2>Step 5: Protect against suspicious messages &amp; content</h2> 
           <p>Hackers can use emails, text messages, phone calls, and web pages to pretend to be institutions, family members, or colleagues.</p> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy">Avoid suspicious requests</h4> 
            <div> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Never give out your passwords. Google will never ask for your password in an email, message, or phone call.</li> 
              <li>Dont reply to suspicious emails, texts, instant messages, webpages, or phone calls that ask for your personal or financial info.</li> 
              <li>Dont click links in emails, messages, webpages, or pop-ups from untrustworthy websites or senders.</li> 
             </ul> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy">Avoid suspicious emails</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p><a href="https://mail.google.com" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Gmail</a> is designed to help protect your account by automatically identifying suspicious emails. You can also use these tips to help you identify suspicious emails and settings:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Check <a href="/mail/answer/180707">if a Gmail message might be fake</a>.</li> 
              <li><a href="/mail/answer/29436">See if the email address and the sender name match.</a></li> 
              <li>If you get a suspicious email in Gmail, report <a href="/mail/answer/1366858">spam</a> or <a href="/mail/answer/8253#report_phishing" rel="noopener">phishing</a>&nbsp;to help us stop similar emails in the future.</li> 
              <li><a href="/mail/answer/7036019#settings">Check your Gmail settings</a> to make sure theres no unfamiliar activity.</li> 
             </ul> 
             <p><strong>Tip:</strong> If you're using Gmail on your computer, point to a link without clicking on it. At the bottom left, look at the web address and make sure it's what you expect.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="zippy-wrapper"> 
            <h4 class="zippy">Avoid suspicious web pages</h4> 
            <div> 
             <p>Google <a href="https://www.google.com/chrome/security/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Chrome</a> and <a href="https://www.google.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Search</a> are designed to warn you about suspicious content and unwanted software.</p> 
             <p>Learn how to manage these warnings in <a href="/chrome/answer/99020">Chrome</a> and <a href="/websearch/answer/45449">Search</a>.</p> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <h2>If you notice suspicious activity on your account</h2> 
           <p>Follow the steps to help <a href="/accounts/answer/6294825">secure your account</a>.</p> 
           <div class="no-margin">
            <h2>Related articles</h2> 
           </div> 
           <div class="no-margin">
            <span id="cke_bm_3171C"></span>
            <ul> 
             <li><a href="https://safety.google/intl/en_us/gmail/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Gmail Security and Privacy Settings</a></li> 
            </ul> 
           </div> 
           <div class="no-margin">
            &nbsp;
           </div> 
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>
